traffic">left</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Telephone numbers in Papua New Guinea">Calling code</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" 3166-2:PG">PG</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.pg" title=".pg">.pg</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Papua New Guinea</b> (<b>PNG</b>; <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/j/: \'y\' in \'yes\'">j</span></span>)<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/u/: \'u\' in \'influence\'">u</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>&#8201;...&#8201;<wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="/&#609;/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">&#609;</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span></span>, <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span></span>-/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/j/: \'y\' in \'yes\'">j</span><span title="/u/: \'u\' in \'influence\'">u</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>, <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/u&#720;/: \'oo\' in \'goose\'">u&#720;</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin_language" title="Tok Pisin language">Tok Pisin</a>: <i lang="tpi">Papua Niugini</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hiri_Motu_language" title="Hiri Motu language">Hiri Motu</a>: <i lang="ho">Papua Niu Gini</i>), officially the <b>Independent State of Papua New Guinea</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceanian</a> country that occupies the eastern half of the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> and its offshore islands in <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a>, a region of the southwestern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> north of Australia. Its capital, located along its southeastern coast, is <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">western half of New Guinea</a> forms the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> provinces of <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">Papua</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West Papua</a>.\n</p><p>At the national level, after being ruled by three external powers since 1884, Papua New Guinea established its sovereignty in 1975. This followed nearly 60 years of Australian administration, which started during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. It became an independent <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a> in 1975 with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> as its <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Monarchy of Papua New Guinea">head of state</a> and became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> in its own right.\n</p><p>Papua New Guinea is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">culturally diverse</a> countries in the world. It is also one of the most rural, as only 18 per cent of its people live in urban centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> There are 852 known <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Languages of Papua New Guinea">languages in the country</a>, of which 12 now have no known living speakers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-5">[5]</a></sup> Most of the population of more than 8 million people lives in <a href="/wiki/Customary_land" title="Customary land">customary communities</a>, which are as diverse as the languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Hawaii_Press_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Hawaii_Press-12">[12]</a></sup> The country is one of the world\'s least explored, culturally and geographically. It is known to have numerous groups of <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples#New_Guinea" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted peoples</a>, and researchers believe there are many undiscovered species of plants and animals in the interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Papua New Guinea is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing economy</a> by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Strong growth in <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Mining in Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea\'s mining and resource sector</a> led to the country becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">sixth-fastest-growing economy</a> in the world in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Growth was expected to slow once major resource projects came on line in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Mining remains a major economic factor, however. Local and national governments are discussing the potential of resuming mining operations at the Panguna mine in <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Bougainville" title="Autonomous Region of Bougainville">Bougainville Province</a>, which has been closed since the civil war in the 1980s&#8211;1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Nearly 40 per cent of the population lives a self-sustainable natural lifestyle with no access to global capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the people still live in strong traditional social groups based on <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">farming</a>. Their social lives combine traditional religion with modern practices, including primary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Hawaii_Press_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Hawaii_Press-12">[12]</a></sup> These societies and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clans" title="Clans">clans</a> are explicitly acknowledged by the Papua New Guinea Constitution, which expresses the wish for "traditional villages and communities to remain as viable units of Papua New Guinean society"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and protects their continuing importance to local and national community life. The nation is an observer state in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> or ASEAN since 1976, and has already filed its application for full membership status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> It is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a> (formerly South Pacific Forum)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> of southeast New Guinea in 1884</div></div></div>\n<p>Archaeological evidence indicates that humans first arrived in Papua New Guinea around 42,000 to 45,000 years ago. They were descendants of migrants out of Africa, in one of the early waves of human migration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agriculture was independently developed in the New Guinea highlands around 7000 BC, making it one of the few areas in the world where people independently domesticated plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A major migration of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_language" title="Austronesian language">Austronesian-speaking</a> peoples to coastal regions of New Guinea took place around 500 BC. This has been correlated with the introduction of pottery, pigs, and certain fishing techniques.\n</p><p>In the 18th century, traders brought the <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a> to New Guinea, where it was adopted and became part of the staples. <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese traders</a> had obtained it from South America and introduced it to the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Moluccas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The far higher crop yields from sweet potato gardens radically transformed traditional agriculture and societies. Sweet potato largely supplanted the previous staple, <a href="/wiki/Colocasia_esculenta" title="Colocasia esculenta">taro</a>, and resulted in a significant increase in population in the highlands.\n</p><p>Although by the late 20th century <a href="/wiki/Headhunting" title="Headhunting">headhunting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a> had been practically eradicated, in the past they were practised in many parts of the country as part of rituals related to warfare and taking in enemy spirits or powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1901, on Goaribari Island in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Papua" title="Gulf of Papua">Gulf of Papua</a>, missionary Harry Dauncey found 10,000 skulls in the island\'s long houses, a demonstration of past practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> According to Marianna Torgovnick, writing in 1991, "The most fully documented instances of cannibalism as a social institution come from New Guinea, where head-hunting and ritual cannibalism survived, in certain isolated areas, into the Fifties, Sixties, and Seventies, and still leave traces within certain social groups."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Little was known in Europe about the island until the 19th century, although <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese and Spanish explorers</a>, such as Dom <a href="/wiki/Jorge_de_Menezes" title="Jorge de Menezes">Jorge de Menezes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Y%C3%B1igo_Ortiz_de_Retez" title="Y&#241;igo Ortiz de Retez">Y&#241;igo Ortiz de Retez</a>, had encountered it as early as the 16th century. Traders from Southeast Asia had visited New Guinea beginning 5,000 years ago to collect <a href="/wiki/Bird-of-paradise" title="Bird-of-paradise">bird-of-paradise</a> plumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country\'s dual name results from its complex administrative history before independence. The word <i>papua</i> is derived from an old local term of uncertain origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tides_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-tides-31">[31]</a></sup> "New Guinea" (<i>Nueva Guinea</i>) was the name <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">coined</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Y%C3%B1igo_Ortiz_de_Retez" title="Y&#241;igo Ortiz de Retez">Y&#241;igo Ortiz de Retez</a>. In 1545, he noted the resemblance of the people to those he had earlier seen along the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">Guinea</a> coast of Africa. Guinea, in its turn, is etymologically derived from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese word</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">Guin&#233;</a></i>. The name is one of several <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponyms</a> sharing similar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Placename_etymology" title="Placename etymology">etymologies</a>, ultimately meaning "land of the blacks" or similar meanings, in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Dark_skin" title="Dark skin">dark skin</a> of the inhabitants.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Guinea_(1884-1919).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="618" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png/220px-New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png/330px-New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png/440px-New_Guinea_%281884-1919%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Guinea_(1884-1919).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New Guinea from 1884 to 1919. <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> controlled the eastern half of New Guinea.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the nineteenth century, Germany ruled the northern half of the country for some decades, beginning in 1884, as a colony named <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a>. In 1914 after the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Australian forces landed and <a href="/wiki/Australian_occupation_of_German_New_Guinea" title="Australian occupation of German New Guinea">captured German New Guinea in a small military campaign</a> and occupied it throughout the war. After the war, in which Germany and the Central Powers were defeated, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> authorised Australia to administer this area as a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> territory.\n</p><p>The southern half of the country had been colonised in 1884 by the United Kingdom as <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Papua" title="Territory of Papua">British New Guinea</a>. With the <a href="/wiki/Papua_Act_1905" title="Papua Act 1905">Papua Act 1905</a>, the UK transferred this territory to the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Commonwealth of Australia</a>, which took on its administration. Additionally, from 1905, British New Guinea was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Papua" title="Territory of Papua">Territory of Papua</a>. In contrast to establishing an Australian mandate in former German New Guinea, the League of Nations determined that Papua was an External Territory of the Australian Commonwealth; as a matter of law it remained a British possession. The difference in legal status meant that until 1949, Papua and New Guinea had entirely separate administrations, both controlled by Australia. These conditions contributed to the complexity of organising the country\'s post-independence legal system.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_(AWM_014008).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg/220px-Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg/330px-Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg/440px-Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_%28AWM_014008%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Australian_infantry_and_armour_at_Buna_(AWM_014008).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Australian forces attack Japanese positions during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buna%E2%80%93Gona" title="Battle of Buna&#8211;Gona">Battle of Buna&#8211;Gona</a>, 7 January 1943.</div></div></div>\n<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea_campaign" title="New Guinea campaign">New Guinea campaign</a> (1942&#8211;1945) was one of the major military campaigns and conflicts between Japan and the Allies. Approximately 216,000 Japanese, Australian, and US servicemen died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> After World War II and the victory of the Allies, the two territories were combined into the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Papua_and_New_Guinea" title="Territory of Papua and New Guinea">Territory of Papua and New Guinea</a>. This was later referred to as "Papua New Guinea".\n</p><p>The natives of Papua appealed to the United Nations for oversight and independence. The nation established independence from <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> on 16 September 1975, becoming a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, continuing to share <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> as its head of state. It maintains close ties with Australia, which continues to be its largest aid donor. Papua New Guinea was admitted to membership in the United Nations on 10 October 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biami_people,_near_Nomad_patrol_post,_1964.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="782" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg/220px-Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg/330px-Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg/440px-Biami_people%2C_near_Nomad_patrol_post%2C_1964.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biami_people,_near_Nomad_patrol_post,_1964.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Australian <a href="/wiki/Kiap" title="Kiap">patrol officer</a> in 1964</div></div></div>\n<p>A secessionist revolt in 1975&#8211;76 on <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville Island</a> resulted in an eleventh-hour modification of the draft <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Law of Papua New Guinea">Constitution of Papua New Guinea</a> to allow for Bougainville and the other eighteen districts to have quasi-federal status as provinces. A renewed <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Civil_War" title="Bougainville Civil War">uprising</a> on Bougainville started in 1988 and claimed 20,000 lives until it was resolved in 1997. Bougainville had been the chief mining region of the country, generating 40% of the national budget. The native peoples felt they were bearing the adverse environmental effects of the mining, which poisoned the land, water and air, without gaining a fair share of the profits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government and rebels negotiated a peace agreement that established the Bougainville Autonomous District and Province. The autonomous Bougainville elected <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabui" title="Joseph Kabui">Joseph Kabui</a> as president in 2005, who served until his death in 2008. He was succeeded by his deputy <a href="/wiki/John_Tabinaman" title="John Tabinaman">John Tabinaman</a> as acting president while an election to fill the unexpired term was organised. <a href="/wiki/James_Tanis" title="James Tanis">James Tanis</a> won that election in December 2008 and served until the inauguration of John Momis, the winner of the 2010 elections. As part of the current peace settlement, a <a href="/wiki/Independence_referendum" title="Independence referendum">referendum on independence</a> is planned to be held in Bougainville sometime before mid-2020. Preparations were underway in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Numerous Chinese have worked and lived in Papua New Guinea, establishing Chinese-majority communities. Chinese merchants became established in the islands before European exploration. <a href="/wiki/Sinophobia" title="Sinophobia">Anti-Chinese</a> rioting involving tens of thousands of people broke out in May 2009. The initial spark was a fight between <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">ethnic Chinese</a> and Papua New Guinean workers at a <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a> factory under construction by a Chinese company. Native resentment against Chinese ownership of numerous small businesses and their commercial monopoly in the islands led to the rioting. The Chinese have long been merchants in Papua New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In the same year, Papua New Guinea asked various Southeast Asian nations for their support for <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Member states of the Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Papua New Guinea\'s full membership bid</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN). <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> supported the bid after Papua New Guinea supported Indonesia\'s hold on <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West Papua</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> have expressed displeasure over Papua New Guinea\'s anti-LGBT laws, stating that equality-friendly <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">Timor-Leste</a> would most likely be a more feasible ASEAN member state in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bt_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-bt-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, despite a refugee crisis at the border of Papua New Guinea and West Papua, the country was steadfast in its support of Indonesia, which promised Papua New Guinea a greater role in ASEAN in the future. By 2017, the Indonesian-led genocide against West Papuan natives peaked with almost 25% of the native population killed within a 50-year period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The realisation caused massive backlash from Oceanian nations against Papua New Guinea\'s policy on West Papua. In January 2017, Papua New Guinea gave citizenship to 138 West Papuan refugees in a bid to calm tensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In September 2017, Papua New Guinea rejected the West Papuan Independence Petition in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, to the pleasure of Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From March to April 2018, <a href="/wiki/2018_Papua_New_Guinea_earthquake" title="2018 Papua New Guinea earthquake">a chain of earthquakes</a> hit Papua New Guinea, causing various damage. Various nations from Oceania, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">Timor-Leste</a> immediately sent aid to the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Politics of Papua New Guinea">Politics of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>. Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is its sovereign and head of state. The constitutional convention, which prepared the draft constitution, and Australia, the outgoing metropolitan power, had thought that Papua New Guinea would not remain a monarchy. The founders, however, considered that imperial honours had a cachet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The monarch is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Governor-General of Papua New Guinea">Governor-General of Papua New Guinea</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dadae" title="Bob Dadae">Bob Dadae</a>. Papua New Guinea (and the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>) are unusual among Commonwealth realms in that governors-general are elected by the legislature, rather than chosen by the executive branch.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Prime Minister of Papua New Guinea">Prime Minister</a> heads the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Cabinet of Papua New Guinea">cabinet</a>, which consists of 31 MPs from the ruling coalition, which make up the government. The current prime minister is <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Neill" title="Peter O\'Neill">Peter O\'Neill</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Parliament_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="National Parliament of Papua New Guinea">National Parliament</a> has 111 seats, of which 22 are occupied by the governors of the 22 provinces and the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_District_(Papua_New_Guinea)" title="National Capital District (Papua New Guinea)">National Capital District</a> (NCD). Candidates for members of parliament are voted upon when the prime minister asks the governor-general to call a national election, a maximum of five years after the previous national election.\n</p><p>In the early years of independence, the instability of the party system led to frequent <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">votes of no confidence</a> in parliament, with resulting changes of the government, but with referral to the electorate, through national elections only occurring every five years. In recent years, successive governments have passed legislation preventing such votes sooner than 18 months after a national election and within 12 months of the next election. In December 2012, the first two (of three) readings were passed to prevent votes of no confidence occurring within the first 30 months. This restriction on votes of no confidence has arguably resulted in greater stability, although perhaps at a cost of reducing the accountability of the executive branch of government.\n</p><p>Elections in PNG attract numerous candidates. After independence in 1975, members were elected by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" title="First past the post">first-past-the-post</a> system, with winners frequently gaining less than 15% of the vote. Electoral reforms in 2001 introduced the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Limited_Preferential_Vote&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Limited Preferential Vote (page does not exist)">Limited Preferential Vote</a> system (LPV), a version of the <a href="/wiki/Instant-runoff_voting" title="Instant-runoff voting">Alternative Vote</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinean_general_election,_2007" title="Papua New Guinean general election, 2007">2007 general election</a> was the first to be conducted using LPV.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1857" data-file-width="1231" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg/170px-Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg/255px-Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg/340px-Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peter_O%27Neill_APEC_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Neill" title="Peter O\'Neill">Peter O\'Neill</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2012</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 2011 there was a <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Papua_New_Guinean_constitutional_crisis" title="2011&#8211;12 Papua New Guinean constitutional crisis">constitutional crisis</a> between the parliament-elect Prime Minister, Peter O\'Neill (voted into office by a large majority of MPs), and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Somare" title="Michael Somare">Sir Michael Somare</a>, who was deemed by the supreme court (in a December Opinion, 3:2) to retain office. The stand-off between parliament and the supreme court continued until the July 2012 national elections, with legislation passed effectively removing the chief justice and subjecting the supreme court members to greater control by the legislature, as well as a series of other laws passed, for example limiting the age for a prime minister. The confrontation reached a peak, with the Deputy Prime Minister entering the supreme court during a hearing, escorted by some police, ostensibly to arrest the Chief Justice. There was strong pressure among some MPs to defer the national elections for a further six months to one year, although their powers to do that were highly questionable.\n</p><p>The parliament-elect prime minister and other cooler-headed MPs carried the votes for the writs for the new election to be issued, slightly late, but for the election itself to occur on time, thereby avoiding a continuation of the constitutional crisis. The crisis was tense at times, but largely restricted to the political and legal fraternity, plus some police factions. The public and public service (including most police and military) stood back. It was a period when, with increased telecommunication access and use of social media (notably Facebook and mobile phones), the public and students played some part in helping maintain restraint and demanding the leadership to adhere to constitutional processes. They insisted on having the elections so that the people could say who should be their legitimate representatives for the next five years.\n</p><p>Under a 2002 amendment, the leader of the party winning the largest number of seats in the election is invited by the governor-general to form the government, if he can muster the necessary majority in parliament. The process of forming such a coalition in PNG, where parties do not have much ideology, involves considerable horsetrading right up until the last moment. Peter O\'Neill emerged as Papua New Guinea\'s prime minister after the July 2012 election, and formed a government with <a href="/wiki/Leo_Dion" title="Leo Dion">Leo Dion</a>, the former Governor of East New Britain Province, as deputy prime minister.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front,_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="851" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg/170px-Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg/255px-Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg/340px-Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front%2C_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_Moresby_parliament_building_front,_by_Steve_Shattuck.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Parliament building of Papua New Guinea in <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Law of Papua New Guinea">Law of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>The unicameral Parliament enacts legislation in the same manner as in other jurisdictions that have "cabinet,"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> "responsible government," or "parliamentary democracy": it is introduced by the executive government to the legislature, debated and, if passed, becomes law when it receives royal assent by the Governor-General. Most legislation is regulation implemented by the bureaucracy under enabling legislation previously passed by Parliament.\n</p><p>All ordinary statutes enacted by Parliament must be consistent with the Constitution. The courts have jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of statutes, both in disputes before them and on a reference where there is no dispute but only an abstract question of law. Unusual among developing countries, the judicial branch of government in Papua New Guinea has remained remarkably independent, and successive executive governments have continued to respect its authority.\n</p><p>The "underlying law" (Papua New Guinea\'s <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>) consists of principles and rules of common law and equity in English<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> common law as it stood on 16 September 1975 (the date of Independence), and thereafter the decisions of PNG\'s own courts. The courts are directed by the Constitution and, latterly, the <i>Underlying Law Act</i>, to take note of the "custom" of traditional communities. They are to determine which customs are common to the whole country and may be declared also to be part of the underlying law. In practice, this has proved extremely difficult and has been largely neglected. Statutes are largely adapted from overseas jurisdictions, primarily Australia and England. Advocacy in the courts follows the adversarial pattern of other common-law countries.\n</p><p>This national court system, used in towns and cities, is supported by a village court system in the more remote areas. The law underpinning the village courts is \'customary law\'.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foreign policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In foreign policy, Papua New Guinea is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, Pacific Islands Forum, and the Melanesian Spearhead Group (MSG) of countries. It was accorded Observer status within <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a> in 1976, followed later by Special Observer status in 1981. It is also a member of <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a> and an <a href="/wiki/African,_Caribbean_and_Pacific_Group_of_States" title="African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States">ACP</a> country, associated with the European Union. The country has a low-key initiative when it comes to the Indonesia-sponsored <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genocide_in_West_Papua" title="Genocide in West Papua">genocide in West Papua</a> due to its application in ASEAN, where the headquarters is in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>.\n</p><p>Papua New Guinea has positive ties with <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and countries in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. It also has good ties with fellow-Christian country, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, especially in the education sector. The country\'s policy has been focusing on ties with Southeast Asia in recent years due to its application in ASEAN, which is supported by the Philippines and co-observer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timor-Leste" title="Timor-Leste">Timor-Leste</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_Defence_Force" title="Papua New Guinea Defence Force">Papua New Guinea Defence Force</a></div>\n<p>The Papua New Guinea Defence Force (PNGDF) is the military organisation responsible for the defence of Papua New Guinea.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinean_children,_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_(21614943268).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3337" data-file-width="5005" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg/220px-Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg/330px-Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg/440px-Papua_New_Guinean_children%2C_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_%2821614943268%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinean_children,_men_and_women_show_their_support_for_putting_an_end_to_violence_against_women_during_a_White_Ribbon_Day_march_(21614943268).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Papua New Guinean children, men and women show their support for putting an end to violence against women during a <a href="/wiki/White_Ribbon_Campaign" title="White Ribbon Campaign">White Ribbon Day</a> march</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Human rights in Papua New Guinea">Human rights in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Sexual violence in Papua New Guinea">Sexual violence in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is often ranked as likely the worst place in the world for <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> A 2013 study in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">The Lancet</a></i> found that 27% of men on Bougainville Island, Papua New Guinea, reported having raped a non-partner, while 14.1% reported having committed <a href="/wiki/Gang_rape" title="Gang rape">gang rape</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, nearly half of reported rape victims are under 15 years of age and 13% are under 7 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICEF2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2-52">[52]</a></sup> A report by <a href="/wiki/ChildFund" title="ChildFund">ChildFund</a> Australia, citing former Parliamentarian Dame <a href="/wiki/Carol_Kidu" title="Carol Kidu">Carol Kidu</a>, claimed 50% of those seeking medical help after rape are under 16, 25% are under 12, and 10% are under 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1976 Sorcery Act imposed a penalty of up to 2 years in prison for the practice of <a href="/wiki/Black_magic" title="Black magic">"black" magic</a>, until the Act was repealed in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> An estimated 50&#8211;150 alleged <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witches</a> are <a href="/wiki/Witch-hunt" title="Witch-hunt">killed</a> each year in Papua New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> There are also no protections given to <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="LGBT rights in Papua New Guinea">LGBT citizens in the country</a>. <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="LGBT rights in Papua New Guinea">Homosexual acts</a> are prohibited by law in Papua New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Regions of Papua New Guinea">Regions of Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Provinces of Papua New Guinea">Provinces of Papua New Guinea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_LLGs_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Districts and LLGs of Papua New Guinea">Districts and LLGs of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is divided into four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="List of regions of Papua New Guinea">regions</a>, which are not the primary administrative divisions but are quite significant in many aspects of government, commercial, sporting and other activities.\n</p><p>The nation has 22 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Provinces of Papua New Guinea">province</a>-level divisions: twenty provinces, the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Bougainville" title="Autonomous Region of Bougainville">Autonomous Region of Bougainville</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_District_(Papua_New_Guinea)" title="National Capital District (Papua New Guinea)">National Capital District</a>. Each province is divided into one or more <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_LLGs_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Districts and LLGs of Papua New Guinea">districts</a>, which in turn are divided into one or more <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_LLGs_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Districts and LLGs of Papua New Guinea">Local-Level Government areas</a>.\n</p><p>Provinces<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> are the primary administrative divisions of the country. Provincial governments are branches of the national government&#8212;Papua New Guinea is not a federation of provinces. The province-level divisions are as follows:\n</p>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Central_Province_(Papua_New_Guinea)" title="Central Province (Papua New Guinea)">Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chimbu_Province" title="Chimbu Province">Chimbu</a> (Simbu)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Highlands_Province" title="Eastern Highlands Province">Eastern Highlands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/East_New_Britain_Province" title="East New Britain Province">East New Britain</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/East_Sepik_Province" title="East Sepik Province">East Sepik</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Enga_Province" title="Enga Province">Enga</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gulf_Province" title="Gulf Province">Gulf</a></li>\n<li><a Province">Western Highlands</a>\n</li><li><a href="/wiki/West_New_Britain_Province" title="West New Britain Province">West New Britain</a>\n</li><li><a href="/wiki/Sandaun_Province" title="Sandaun Province">Jiwaka</a>\n</li></ol>\n</td>\n<td style="width:315px; vertical-align:middle;">\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image"
