class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papua_new_guinea_provinces_(numbers)_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Provinces of Papua New Guinea.</div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 2009, Parliament approved the creation of two additional provinces: <a href="/wiki/Hela_Province" title="Hela Province">Hela Province</a>, consisting of part of the existing <a href="/wiki/Southern_Highlands_Province" title="Southern Highlands Province">Southern Highlands Province</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jiwaka_Province" title="Jiwaka Province">Jiwaka Province</a>, formed by dividing <a href="/wiki/Western_Highlands_Province" title="Western Highlands Province">Western Highlands Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Jiwaka and Hela officially became separate provinces on 17 May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The declaration of Hela and Jiwaka is a result of the largest <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> (LNG)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> project in the country that is situated in both provinces. The government set 15 June 2019 as the voting date for an independence referendum in the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Bougainville" title="Autonomous Region of Bougainville">Bougainville (autonomous region)</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Strategic_Policy_Institute" title="Australian Strategic Policy Institute">Australian Strategic Policy Institute</a> has said that there is a wide expectation Bougainville will vote to become independent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Geography of Papua New Guinea">Geography of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:324px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinea_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="322" decoding="async" height="346" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/Papua_New_Guinea_map.png" width="322"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption">Map of Papua New Guinea</div></div></div>\n<p>At 462,840&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (178,704&#160;sq&#160;mi), Papua New Guinea is the world\'s fifty-fourth-largest country. Including all its islands, it lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">0&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_south" title="12th parallel south">12&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_east" title="140th meridian east">140&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/160th_meridian_east" title="160th meridian east">160&#176;E</a>.\n</p><p>Located north of the Australian mainland, the country\'s geography is diverse and, in places, extremely rugged. A spine of mountains, the <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea_Highlands" title="New Guinea Highlands">New Guinea Highlands</a>, runs the length of the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, forming a populous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highland_(geography)" title="Highland (geography)">highlands</a> region mostly covered with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a>, and the long <a href="/wiki/Papuan_Peninsula" title="Papuan Peninsula">Papuan Peninsula</a>, known as the \'Bird\'s Tail\'. Dense <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a> can be found in the lowland and coastal areas as well as very large <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetland</a> areas surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Sepik" title="Sepik">Sepik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fly_River" title="Fly River">Fly</a> rivers. This terrain has made it difficult for the country to develop transportation infrastructure. Some areas are accessible only on foot or by aeroplane.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Wilhelm" title="Mount Wilhelm">Mount Wilhelm</a> at 4,509 metres (14,793&#160;ft). Papua New Guinea is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> which are under close watch, in the interests of preservation.\n</p><p>The country is situated on the Pacific <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, at the point of collision of several <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic plates</a>. There are a number of active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a>, and eruptions are frequent. Earthquakes are relatively common, sometimes accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunamis</a>.\n</p><p>The mainland of the country is the eastern half of New Guinea island, where the largest towns are also located, including <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a> (capital) and <a href="/wiki/Lae" title="Lae">Lae</a>; other major islands within Papua New Guinea include <a href="/wiki/New_Ireland_(island)" title="New Ireland (island)">New Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">New Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manus_Island" title="Manus Island">Manus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a>.\n</p><p>Papua New Guinea is one of the few regions close to the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> that experience <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snowfall</a>, which occurs in the most elevated parts of the mainland.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borders">Borders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Borders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The border between Papua New Guinea and Indonesia was confirmed by treaty with Australia before independence in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bordertreaty1974_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-bordertreaty1974-62">[62]</a></sup>  The land border comprises a segment of the <a href="/wiki/141st_meridian_east" title="141st meridian east">141&#176; E meridian</a> from the north coast southwards to where it meets the <a href="/wiki/Fly_River" title="Fly River">Fly River</a> flowing east, then a short curve of the river\'s <a href="/wiki/Thalweg" title="Thalweg">thalweg</a> to where it meets the 141&#176;01\'10" E meridian flowing west, then southwards to the south coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bordertreaty1974_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-bordertreaty1974-62">[62]</a></sup> The 141&#176; E meridian formed the entire eastern boundary of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_New_Guinea" title="Dutch New Guinea">Dutch New Guinea</a> according to its 1828 annexation proclamation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VanderVeur1966_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-VanderVeur1966-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_The_Hague_(1895)" title="Treaty of The Hague (1895)">In 1895</a> the Dutch and British agreed to a territorial exchange, bringing the entire left bank of the Fly River into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_New_Guinea" title="British New Guinea">British New Guinea</a> and moving the southern border east to the <a href="/wiki/Torasi_Estuary" title="Torasi Estuary">Torasi Estuary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VanderVeur1966_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-VanderVeur1966-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The maritime boundary with Australia was confirmed by a treaty in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">Torres Strait</a> it runs close to the mainland of New Guinea, keeping the adjacent North Western <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islands" title="Torres Strait Islands">Torres Strait Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dauan_Island" title="Dauan Island">Dauan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boigu_Island_(Queensland)" title="Boigu Island (Queensland)">Boigu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saibai_Island" title="Saibai Island">Saibai</a>) under Australian sovereignty. Maritime boundaries with the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> were confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea%E2%80%93Solomon_Islands_Maritime_Boundary_Treaty" title="Papua New Guinea&#8211;Solomon Islands Maritime Boundary Treaty">a 1989 treaty</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Conservation_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Conservation in Papua New Guinea">Conservation in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tarvurvur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Tarvurvur.jpg/220px-Tarvurvur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Tarvurvur.jpg/330px-Tarvurvur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Tarvurvur.jpg/440px-Tarvurvur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tarvurvur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mount <a href="/wiki/Tavurvur" title="Tavurvur">Tavurvur</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinea_(5986599443).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg/220px-Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg/330px-Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg/440px-Papua_New_Guinea_%285986599443%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinea_(5986599443).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Papua New Guinea\'s highlands</div></div></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is part of the <a href="/wiki/Australasian_realm" title="Australasian realm">Australasia ecozone</a>, which also includes Australia, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, eastern <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and several Pacific island groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>.\n</p><p>Geologically, the island of New Guinea is a northern extension of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Australian_Plate" title="Indo-Australian Plate">Indo-Australian tectonic plate</a>, forming part of a single land mass which is <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">Australia-New Guinea</a> (also called <i>Sahul</i> or <i>Meganesia</i>). It is connected to the Australian segment by a shallow <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">Torres Strait</a>, which in former ages lay exposed as a <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a>, particularly during <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice ages</a> when sea levels were lower than at present.\n</p><p>Consequently, many species of birds and mammals found on New Guinea have close genetic links with corresponding species found in Australia. One notable feature in common for the two landmasses is the existence of several species of <a href="/wiki/Marsupial" title="Marsupial">marsupial</a> <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a>, including some <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">kangaroos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phalangeriformes" title="Phalangeriformes">possums</a>, which are not found elsewhere. Papua New Guinea is a <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse country</a>.\n</p><p>Many of the other islands within PNG territory, including New Britain, New Ireland, Bougainville, the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Islands" title="Admiralty Islands">Admiralty Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Trobriand_Islands" title="Trobriand Islands">Trobriand Islands</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Louisiade_Archipelago" title="Louisiade Archipelago">Louisiade Archipelago</a>, were never linked to New Guinea by land bridges. As a consequence, they have their own flora and fauna; in particular, they lack many of the land mammals and flightless birds that are common to New Guinea and Australia.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg/220px-Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg/330px-Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg/440px-Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baby_tree_kangaroo_on_the_chiefs_wifes_shoulder_-Papua_New_Guinea-17Oct2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Tree-kangaroo" title="Tree-kangaroo">tree-kangaroo</a> in Papua New Guinea</div></div></div>\n<p>Australia and New Guinea are portions of the ancient supercontinent of <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a>, which started to break into smaller continents in the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> era, 66&#8211;130 million years ago. Australia finally broke free from <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> about 45 million years ago. All the Australasian lands are home to the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_flora" title="Antarctic flora">Antarctic flora</a>, descended from the flora of southern Gondwana, including the <a href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">coniferous</a> <a href="/wiki/Podocarpaceae" title="Podocarpaceae">podocarps</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Araucaria" title="Araucaria">Araucaria</a></i> pines, and the broadleafed southern beech (<i><a href="/wiki/Nothofagus" title="Nothofagus">Nothofagus</a></i>). These plant families are still present in Papua New Guinea.\n</p><p>As the Indo-Australian Plate (which includes landmasses of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, Australia, and the Indian Ocean floor in between) drifts north, it collides with the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>. The collision of the two plates pushed up the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, the Indonesian islands, and New Guinea\'s Central Range. The Central Range is much younger and higher than the mountains of Australia, so high that it is home to rare equatorial <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a>. New Guinea is part of the humid tropics, and many <a href="/wiki/Indomalayan_realm" title="Indomalayan realm">Indomalayan</a> rainforest plants spread across the narrow straits from Asia, mixing together with the old Australian and Antarctic floras.\n</p><p>PNG includes a number of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Islands" title="Admiralty Islands">Admiralty Islands</a> lowland rain forests &#8211; forested islands to the north of the mainland, home to a distinct flora.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_Guinea_Highlands" title="New Guinea Highlands">Central Range montane rain forests</a><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PNG-climate.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="662" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/PNG-climate.png/220px-PNG-climate.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/PNG-climate.png/330px-PNG-climate.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/PNG-climate.png/440px-PNG-climate.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PNG-climate.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Green <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a> of Papua New Guinea bears a sharp contrast to nearby <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> Australia.</div></div></div></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Huon_Peninsula" title="Huon Peninsula">Huon Peninsula</a> montane rain forests</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Louisiade_Archipelago" title="Louisiade Archipelago">Louisiade Archipelago</a> rain forests</li>\n<li>New Britain-New Ireland lowland rain forests</li>\n<li>New Britain-New Ireland montane rain forests</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_Guinea_mangroves" title="New Guinea mangroves">New Guinea mangroves</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_New_Guinea_lowland_rain_and_freshwater_swamp_forests" title="Northern New Guinea lowland rain and freshwater swamp forests">Northern New Guinea lowland rain and freshwater swamp forests</a></li>\n<li>Northern New Guinea montane rain forests</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_rain_forests" title="Solomon Islands rain forests">Solomon Islands rain forests</a> (includes Bougainville Island and Buka)</li>\n<li>Southeastern Papuan rain forests</li>\n<li>Southern New Guinea freshwater swamp forests</li>\n<li>Southern New Guinea lowland rain forests</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Trobriand_Islands_rain_forests" title="Trobriand Islands rain forests">Trobriand Islands rain forests</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Trans_Fly_savanna_and_grasslands" title="Trans Fly savanna and grasslands">Trans Fly savanna and grasslands</a></li>\n<li>Central Range sub-alpine grasslands</li></ul>\n<p>Three new species of mammals were discovered in the forests of Papua New Guinea by an Australian-led expedition. A small wallaby, a large-eared mouse and shrew-like marsupial were discovered. The expedition was also successful in capturing photographs and video footage of some other rare animals such as the <a href="/wiki/Tenkile" title="Tenkile">Tenkile</a> tree kangaroo and the Weimang tree kangaroo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Environmental issues in Papua New Guinea">Environmental issues in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>At <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Deforestation in Papua New Guinea">current rates of deforestation</a>, more than half of Papua New Guinea\'s forests could be lost or seriously degraded by 2021, according to a new satellite study of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Nearly one quarter of Papua New Guinea\'s rainforests were damaged or destroyed between 1972 and 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_earthquake">2018 earthquake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2018 earthquake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_Papua_New_Guinea_earthquake" title="2018 Papua New Guinea earthquake">2018 Papua New Guinea earthquake</a></div>\n<p>On February 25, 2018, an earthquake of magnitude 7.5 and depth of 35 kilometres struck the middle of Papua New Guinea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The worst of the damage was centred around the Southern Highlands region. As of March 1 there were 31 reported deaths, and that number was expected to rise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Economy of Papua New Guinea">Economy of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2472" data-file-width="3296" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg/220px-Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg/330px-Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg/440px-Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Place_Port_Moresby_November_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Port Moresby\'s central business district</div></div></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is richly endowed with natural resources, including mineral and renewable resources, such as forests, marine (including a large portion of the world\'s major tuna stocks), and in some parts agriculture. The rugged terrain&#8212;including high mountain ranges and valleys, swamps and islands&#8212;and high cost of developing infrastructure, combined with other factors (including serious law and order problems in some centres and the system of customary land title) makes it difficult for outside developers. Local developers are handicapped by years of deficient investment in education, health, ICT and access to finance. Agriculture, for subsistence and cash crops, provides a livelihood for 85% of the population and continues to provide some 30% of GDP. Mineral deposits, including gold, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a>, and copper, account for 72% of export earnings. <a href="/wiki/Elaeis_guineensis" title="Elaeis guineensis">Oil palm</a> production has grown steadily over recent years (largely from estates and with extensive outgrower output), with <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> now the main agricultural export. In households participating, coffee remains the major export crop (produced largely in the Highlands provinces), followed by <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">coconut oil</a>/<a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> from the coastal areas, each largely produced by smallholders and tea, produced on estates and rubber. The Iagifu/Hedinia Field was discovered in 1986 in the Papuan <a href="/wiki/Fold_and_thrust_belt" title="Fold and thrust belt">fold and thrust belt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matzke_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Matzke-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>471</span></sup>\n</p><p>Former Prime Minister Sir <a href="/wiki/Mekere_Morauta" title="Mekere Morauta">Mekere Morauta</a> tried to restore integrity to state institutions, stabilise the <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinean_kina" title="Papua New Guinean kina">kina</a>, restore stability to the national budget, privatise public enterprises where appropriate, and ensure ongoing peace on Bougainville following the 1997 agreement which ended <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a>\'s secessionist unrest. The Morauta government had considerable success in attracting international support, specifically gaining the backing of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in securing development assistance loans. Significant challenges face Prime Minister Sir <a href="/wiki/Michael_Somare" title="Michael Somare">Michael Somare</a>, including gaining further investor confidence, continuing efforts to privatise government assets, and maintaining the support of members of Parliament.\n</p><p>In March 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> Policy called for Papua New Guinea\'s designation of developing country to be downgraded to least-developed country because of protracted economic and social stagnation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> However, an evaluation by the IMF in late 2008 found that "a combination of prudent fiscal and monetary policies, and high global prices for mineral commodity exports, have underpinned Papua New Guinea\'s recent buoyant economic growth and macroeconomic stability. By 2012 PNG had enjoyed a decade of positive economic growth, at over 6% since 2007, even during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Crisis" title="Global Financial Crisis">Global Financial Crisis</a> years of 2008/9. PNG\'s Real GDP growth rate as at 2011 was 8.9%,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and 9.2% for 2012, according to the Asian Development Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-investvine_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-investvine-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This economic growth has been primarily attributed to strong commodity prices, particularly mineral but also agricultural, with the high demand for mineral products largely sustained even during the crisis by the buoyant Asian markets, <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Mining in Papua New Guinea">a booming mining sector</a>, and particularly since 2009<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> by a buoyant outlook and the construction phase for natural gas exploration, production, and exportation in liquefied form (<a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> or "LNG") by LNG tankers (<a href="/wiki/LNG_carrier" title="LNG carrier">LNG carrier</a>), all of which will require multibillion-dollar investments (exploration, production wells, pipelines, storage, liquefaction plants, port terminals, LNG tanker ships).\n</p><p>The first major gas project was the PNG LNG joint venture. <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a> is operator of the joint venture, also comprising PNG company <a href="/wiki/Oil_Search" title="Oil Search">Oil Search</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santos_Limited" title="Santos Limited">Santos</a>, Kumul Petroleum Holdings (Papua New Guinea&#8217;s national oil and gas company), <a href="/wiki/JXTG_Holdings" title="JXTG Holdings">JX Nippon Oil and Gas Exploration</a>, the PNG government\'s <a href="/wiki/Mineral_Resources_Development_Company" title="Mineral Resources Development Company">Mineral Resources Development Company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petromin_Corporation" title="Petromin Corporation">Petromin PNG Holdings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exxon_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exxon-74">[74]</a></sup> The project is an integrated development that includes gas production and processing facilities in the <a href="/wiki/Hela_Province" title="Hela Province">Hela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Highlands_Province" title="Southern Highlands Province">Southern Highlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Province_(Papua_New_Guinea)" title="Western Province (Papua New Guinea)">Western</a> Provinces of Papua New Guinea, including liquefaction and storage facilities (located northwest of Port Moresby) with capacity of 6.9 million tonnes per year. There are over 700 kilometres (430&#160;mi) of pipelines connecting the facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exxon_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Exxon-74">[74]</a></sup> It is the largest private-sector investment in the history of PNG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A second major project is based on initial rights held by the French oil and gas major <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">Total S.A.</a> and the US company <a href="/wiki/InterOil" title="InterOil">InterOil</a> Corp. (IOC), which have partly combined their assets after Total agreed in December 2013 to purchase 61.3% of IOC\'s Antelope and Elk gas field rights, with the plan to develop them starting in 2016, including the construction of a liquefaction plant to allow export of LNG. Total S.A. has separately another joint operating agreement with <a href="/wiki/Oil_Search" title="Oil Search">Oil Search</a>.\n</p><p>Further gas and mineral projects are proposed (including the large Wafi-Golpu copper-gold mine), with extensive exploration ongoing across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Economic \'development\' based on the extractive industries carries difficult consequences for local communities. There has been much contention<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> around river tailings in the vast Fly River,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> submarine tailings from the new Ramu-Nickel-cobalt mine, commencing exports in late 2012 (after a delay from landowner-led court challenges),<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and from proposed submarine mining in the Bismarck Sea (by <a href="/wiki/Nautilus_Minerals" title="Nautilus Minerals">Nautilus Minerals</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> One major project conducted through the PNG Department for Community Development suggested that other pathways to sustainable development should be considered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The PNG government\'s long-term Vision 2050 and shorter-term policy documents, including the 2013 Budget and the 2014 Responsible Sustainable Development Strategy, emphasise the need for a more diverse economy, based upon sustainable industries and avoiding the effects of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_disease" title="Dutch disease">Dutch disease</a> from major resource extraction projects undermining other industries, as has occurred in many countries experiencing oil or other mineral booms, notably in Western Africa, undermining much of their agriculture sector, manufacturing and tourism, and with them broad-based employment prospects. Measures have been taken to mitigate these effects, including through the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund" title="Sovereign wealth fund">sovereign wealth fund</a>, partly to stabilise revenue and expenditure flows, but much will depend upon the readiness to make real reforms to effective use of revenue, tackling rampant corruption and empowering households and businesses to access markets, services and develop a more buoyant economy, with lower costs, especially for small to medium-size enterprises.\n</p><p>The Institute of National Affairs, a PNG independent policy think tank, provides a report on the business and investment environment of Papua New Guinea every five years, based upon a survey of large and small, local and overseas companies, highlighting law and order problems and corruption, as the worst impediments, followed by the poor state of transport, power and communications infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_tenure">Land tenure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Land tenure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OkTediMine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/OkTediMine.jpg/220px-OkTediMine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/OkTediMine.jpg/330px-OkTediMine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/OkTediMine.jpg/440px-OkTediMine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OkTediMine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ok_Tedi_Mine" title="Ok Tedi Mine">Ok Tedi Mine</a> in southwestern Papua New Guinea</div></div></div>\n<p>The PNG legislature has enacted laws in which a type of tenure called "<a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_title" title="Aboriginal title">customary land title</a>" is recognised, meaning that the traditional lands of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> have some legal basis to inalienable tenure. This customary land notionally covers most of the usable land in the country (some 97% of total land area);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alienated_land" title="Alienated land">alienated land</a> is either held privately under state lease or is government land. Freehold title (also known as <a href="/wiki/Fee_simple" title="Fee simple">fee simple</a>) can only be held by Papua New Guinean citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only some 3% of the land of Papua New Guinea is in private hands; this is privately held under 99-year state lease, or it is held by the State. There is virtually no freehold title; the few existing freeholds are automatically converted to state lease when they are transferred between vendor and purchaser. Unalienated land is owned under customary title by traditional landowners. The precise nature of the <a href="/wiki/Seisin" title="Seisin">seisin</a> varies from one culture to another. Many writers portray land as in the communal ownership of traditional clans; however, closer studies usually show that the smallest portions of land whose ownership cannot be further divided are held by the individual heads of extended families and their descendants or their descendants alone if they have recently died.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>This is a matter of vital importance because a problem of economic development is identifying the membership of customary landowning groups and the owners. Disputes between mining and forestry companies and landowner groups often devolve on the issue of whether the companies entered into contractual relations for the use of land with the true owners. Customary property&#8212;usually land&#8212;cannot be devised by will. It can only be inherited according to the custom of the deceased\'s people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Lands Act was amended in 2010 along with the Land Group Incorporation Act, intended to improve the management of state land, mechanisms for dispute resolution over land, and to enable customary landowners to be better able to access finance and possible partnerships over portions of their land, if they seek to develop it for urban or rural economic activities. The Land Group Incorporation Act requires more specific identification of the customary landowners than hitherto and their more specific authorisation before any land arrangements are determined; (a major issue in recent years has been a land grab, using, or rather misusing, the Lease-Leaseback provision under the Land Act, notably using \'Special Agricultural and Business Leases\' (SABLs) to acquire vast tracts of customary land, purportedly for agricultural projects, but in an almost all cases as a back-door mechanism for securing tropical forest resources for logging&#8212;circumventing the more exacting requirements of the Forest Act, for securing Timber Permits (which must comply with sustainability requirements and be competitively secured, and with the customary landowners approval). Following a national outcry, these SABLs have been subject to a Commission of Inquiry, established in mid-2011, for which the report is still awaited for initial presentation to the Prime Minister and Parliament.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Demographics of Papua New Guinea">Demographics of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.6\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">8.1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Papua New Guinea is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Homogeneity_and_heterogeneity" title="Homogeneity and heterogeneity">heterogeneous</a> nations in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fearon_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-fearon-82">[82]</a></sup> There are hundreds of ethnic groups indigenous to Papua New Guinea, the majority being from the group known as <a href="/wiki/Papuan_people" title="Papuan people">Papuans</a>, whose ancestors arrived in the New Guinea region tens of thousands of years ago. The other indigenous peoples are <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesians</a>, their ancestors having arrived in the region less than four thousand years ago.\n</p><p>There are also numerous people from other parts of the world now resident, including <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Chinese people in Papua New Guinea">Chinese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Europeans, Australians, Indonesians, Filipinos, Polynesians, and Micronesians (the last four belonging to the Austronesian family). Around 40,000 expatriates, mostly from Australia and China, were living in Papua New Guinea in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Urbanisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="10"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float: Highlands</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">18,503\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p><br/>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Huli_wigman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Huli_wigman.jpg/220px-Huli_wigman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Huli_wigman.jpg/330px-Huli_wigman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Huli_wigman.jpg/440px-Huli_wigman.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Huli_wigman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Huli_people" title="Huli people">Huli</a> wigman from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Highlands,_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Southern Highlands, Papua New Guinea">Southern Highlands</a></div></div></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Languages of Papua New Guinea">Languages of Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TNG_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/TNG_map.svg/220px-TNG_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/TNG_map.svg/330px-TNG_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/TNG_map.svg/440px-TNG_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TNG_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The language families in Ross\'s conception of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-New_Guinea" title="Trans-New Guinea">Trans-New Guinea</a> language family</div></div></div>\n<p>Papua New Guinea has more languages than any other country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> with over 820 indigenous languages, representing 12% of the world\'s total, but most have fewer than 1,000 speakers. The most widely spoken indigenous language is <a href="/wiki/Enga_language" title="Enga language">Enga</a>, with about 200,000 speakers, followed by <a href="/wiki/Melpa_language" title="Melpa language">Melpa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huli_language" title="Huli language">Huli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Indigenous languages are classified into two large groups, <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a> and non-Austronesian, or <a href="/wiki/Papuan_languages" title="Papuan languages">Papuan</a>, languages. There are four official languages in Papua New Guinea: English, sign language (which in practice means <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinean_Sign_Language" title="Papua New Guinean Sign Language">Papua New Guinean Sign Language</a>), <a href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin" title="Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiri_Motu" title="Hiri Motu">Hiri Motu</a>.\n</p><p>English is the language of government and the education system, but it is not spoken widely.\n</p><p>The primary <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the country is <a href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin" title="Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a> (commonly known in English as New Guinean Pidgin or Melanesian Pidgin), in which much of the debate in Parliament is conducted, many information campaigns and advertisements are presented, and until recently a national newspaper, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wantok&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wantok (page does not exist)">Wantok</a></i>, was published. The only area where Tok Pisin is not prevalent is the southern region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papua_region" title="Papua region">Papua</a>, where people often use the third official language, <a href="/wiki/Hiri_Motu" title="Hiri Motu">Hiri Motu</a>.\n</p><p>Although it lies in the Papua region, Port Moresby has a highly diverse population which primarily uses Tok Pisin, and to a lesser extent English, with Motu spoken as the indigenous language in outlying villages. With an average of only 7,000 speakers per language, Papua New Guinea has a greater density of languages than any other nation on earth except <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>See <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Health in Papua New Guinea">Health in Papua New Guinea</a>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Religion in Papua New Guinea">Religion in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 272.37868371333px 100px 0; border-right-color:#377eb8"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:#377eb8"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 6.291466725365px 100px 0; border-right-color:#e41a1c"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:#e41a1c"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Citizen population in Papua New Guinea by religion, based on the 2011 census<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #e41a1c; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (26%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #377eb8; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea</a> (18.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #984ea3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a> (12.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff7f00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> (10.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4daf4a; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Church_in_Papua_New_Guinea_and_the_Solomon_Islands" title="United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands">United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands</a> (10.3%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a65628; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Alliance" title="Evangelical Alliance">Evangelical Alliance</a> Papua New Guinea (5.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Violet; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Anglican Church of Papua New Guinea">Anglican Church of Papua New Guinea</a> (3.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> (2.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> (0.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Cyan; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Kwato Church (0.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (5.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non Christian (1.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Not stated (3.1%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>The courts and government practice uphold the constitutional right to freedom of speech, thought, and belief, and no legislation to curb those rights has been adopted. The 2011 census found that 95.6% of citizens identified themselves as members of a Christian church, 1.4% were not Christian, 3.1% did not answer this census question. These who stated no religion accounted for, approximately, 0%. Many citizens combine their Christian faith with some traditional indigenous religious practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christianity in Papua New Guinea is predominantly made up of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, who collectively constitute roughly 70% of the total population. They are mostly represented by the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, diverse <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a> denominations, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Church_in_Papua_New_Guinea_and_the_Solomon_Islands" title="United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands">United Church in Papua New Guinea and the Solomon Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Alliance" title="Evangelical Alliance">Evangelical Alliance</a> Papua New Guinea, and the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Anglican Church of Papua New Guinea">Anglican Church of Papua New Guinea</a>. Apart from Protestants, there is a notable <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> minority with approximately 25% of the population.\n</p><p>There are approximately 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Islam in Papua New Guinea">Muslims in the country</a>. The majority belong to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> group, while a small number are <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadi</a>. Non-traditional Christian churches and non-Christian religious groups are active throughout the country. The <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_Council_of_Churches" title="Papua New Guinea Council of Churches">Papua New Guinea Council of Churches</a> has stated that both Muslim and Confucian missionaries are active, and foreign missionary activity in general is high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Traditional religions are often <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animist" title="Animist">animist</a>. Some also tend to have elements of <a href="/wiki/Veneration_of_the_dead" title="Veneration of the dead">veneration of the dead</a>, though generalisation is suspect given the extreme heterogeneity of Melanesian societies. Prevalent among traditional tribes is the belief in <i>masalai</i>, or evil spirits, which are blamed for "poisoning" people, causing calamity and death, and the practice of puripuri (<a href="/wiki/Maleficium_(sorcery)" title="Maleficium (sorcery)">sorcery</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Culture of Papua New Guinea">Culture of Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Music of Papua New Guinea">Music of Papua New Guinea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinean_cuisine" title="Papua New Guinean cuisine">Papua New Guinean cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PNG_Bilum_Bag_QM_r.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/PNG_Bilum_Bag_QM_r.jpg/220px-PNG_Bilum_Bag_QM_r.jpg" href="/wiki/File:Papua_New_Guinean.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A resident of Boga-Boga, a village on the southeast coast of mainland Papua New Guinea</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thiafamous_4318b.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiafamous_4318b.JPG/220px-Thiafamous_4318b.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiafamous_4318b.JPG/330px-Thiafamous_4318b.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Thiafamous_4318b.JPG/440px-Thiafamous_4318b.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thiafamous_4318b.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Asaro_Mudmen" title="Asaro Mudmen">Asaro Mudmen</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1127" decoding="async" height="343" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG/170px-Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG/255px-Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG/340px-Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abelam_wooden_ancestor_figure_2_CAC.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 20th-century wooden <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abelam" title="Abelam">Abelam</a> ancestor figure (<i>nggwalndu</i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>It is estimated that more than a thousand cultural groups exist in Papua New Guinea. Because of this diversity, many styles of cultural expression have emerged. Each group has created its own expressive forms in art, dance, weaponry, costumes, singing, music, architecture and much more.\n</p><p>Most of these cultural groups have their own language. People typically live in villages that rely on subsistence farming. In some areas people hunt and collect wild plants (such as <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yam roots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karuka" title="Karuka">karuka</a>) to supplement their diets. Those who become skilled at hunting, farming and fishing earn a great deal of respect.\n</p><p>On the <a href="/wiki/Sepik" title="Sepik">Sepik</a> river, there is a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Wood_carving" title="Wood carving">wood carving</a>, often in the form of plants or animals, representing <a href="/wiki/Ancestor" title="Ancestor">ancestor</a> spirits.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Seashell" title="Seashell">Seashells</a> are no longer the currency of Papua New Guinea, as they were in some regions&#8212;sea shells were abolished as currency in 1933. This tradition is still present in local customs. In some cultures, to get a bride, a groom must bring a certain number of golden-edged clam shells<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> as a <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a>. In other regions, the bride price is paid in lengths of <a href="/wiki/Shell_money" title="Shell money">shell money</a>, pigs, <a href="/wiki/Cassowary" title="Cassowary">cassowaries</a> or cash. Elsewhere, it is brides who traditionally pay a <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a>.\n</p><p>People of the highlands engage in colourful local rituals that are called "sing sings". They paint themselves and dress up with <a href="/wiki/Feather" title="Feather">feathers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl" title="Pearl">pearls</a> and animal skins to represent birds, trees or mountain spirits. Sometimes an important event, such as a legendary battle, is enacted at such a musical festival.\n</p><p>The country possesses one (1) <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>, namely, <a href="/wiki/Kuk_Swamp" title="Kuk Swamp">Kuk Early Agricultural Site</a>, which was inscribed in 2008. The country, however, has no elements inscribed yet in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists</a>, despite having one of the widest array of intangible cultural heritage elements in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Sport in Papua New Guinea">Sport in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>Sport is an important part of Papua New Guinean culture and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> is by far the most popular sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In a nation where communities are far apart and many people live at a minimal subsistence level, rugby league has been described as a replacement for tribal warfare as a way of explaining the local enthusiasm for the game (a matter of life or death). Many Papua New Guineans have become instant celebrities by representing their country or playing in an overseas professional league. Even Australian rugby league players who have played in the annual <a href="/wiki/State_of_Origin_series" title="State of Origin series">State of Origin series</a>, which is celebrated feverishly every year in PNG, are among the most well-known people throughout the nation.\n</p><p>State of Origin is a highlight of the year for most Papua New Guineans, although the support is so passionate that many people have died over the years in violent clashes supporting their team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_national_rugby_league_team" title="Papua New Guinea national rugby league team">Papua New Guinea national rugby league team</a> usually plays against the Australian Prime Minister\'s XIII (a selection of NRL players) each year, normally in Port Moresby.\n</p><p>Although not as popular, <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> is more significant in another way, as <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_national_Australian_rules_football_team" title="Papua New Guinea national Australian rules football team">the national team</a> is ranked second, only after Australia. Other major sports which have a part in the Papua New Guinea sporting landscape are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> and, in eastern Papua, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>.\n</p><p>The capital city, Port Moresby, hosted the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Games" title="Pacific Games">Pacific Games</a> in 2015.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Education in Papua New Guinea">Education in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>A large proportion of the population is <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">illiterate</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-99">[99]</a></sup> with women predominating in this area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-99">[99]</a></sup> Much of the education in PNG is provided by church institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> This includes 500 schools of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Papua New Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Papua New Guinea has six universities apart from other major tertiary institutions. The two founding universities are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="University of Papua New Guinea">University of Papua New Guinea</a>, based in the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_District_(Papua_New_Guinea)" title="National Capital District (Papua New Guinea)">National Capital District</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_University_of_Technology" title="Papua New Guinea University of Technology">Papua New Guinea University of Technology</a>, based outside of <a href="/wiki/Lae" title="Lae">Lae</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Morobe_Province" title="Morobe Province">Morobe Province</a>.\n</p><p>The four other universities which were once colleges were established recently after gaining government recognition. These are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Goroka" title="University of Goroka">University of Goroka</a> in the Eastern Highlands province, <a href="/wiki/Divine_Word_University" title="Divine Word University">Divine Word University</a> (run by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Society_of_the_Divine_Word" title="Society of the Divine Word">Divine Word Missionaries</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Madang_Province" title="Madang Province">Madang Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea_University_of_Natural_Resources_and_Environment" title="Papua New Guinea University of Natural Resources and Environment">Vudal University</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_New_Britain_Province" title="East New Britain Province">East New Britain Province</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Adventist_University" title="Pacific Adventist University">Pacific Adventist University</a> (run by the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>) in the National Capital District.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Papua New Guinea\'s <i>National Vision 2050</i> was adopted in 2009. This has led to the establishment of the Research, Science and Technology Council. At its gathering in November 2014, the Council re-emphasised the need to focus on sustainable development through <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Pacific_Island_countries" title="Science and technology in Pacific Island countries">science and technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Vision 2050</i>\'s medium-term priorities are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>emerging industrial technology for downstream processing;</li>\n<li>infrastructure technology for the economic corridors;</li>\n<li>knowledge-based technology;</li>\n<li>Science and engineering education; and</li>\n<li>to reach the target of investing 5% of GDP in research and development by 2050. (There is no recent data for this indicator.)</li></ul>\n<p>According to Thomson Reuters\' Web of Science, Papua New Guinea had the largest number of publications (110) among Pacific Island states in 2014, followed by Fiji (106). Nine out of ten scientific publications from Papua New Guinea focused on immunology, genetics, biotechnology and microbiology. Nine out of ten were also co-authored by scientists from other countries, mainly Australia, the United States of America, United Kingdom, Spain and Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Forestry is an important economic resource for Papua New Guinea but the industry uses low and semi-intensive technological inputs. As a result, product ranges are limited to sawed timber, veneer, plywood, block board, moulding, poles and posts and wood chips. Only a few limited finished products are exported. Lack of automated machinery, coupled with inadequately trained local technical personnel, are some of the obstacles to introducing automated machinery and design. Policy-makers need to turn their attention to eliminating these barriers, in order for forestry to make a more efficient and sustainable contribution to national economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Papua New Guinea, renewable energy sources represent two-thirds of the total electricity supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-4"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup> In 2015, the Secretariat of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a> observed that, \'while Fiji, Papua New Guinea and Samoa are leading the way with large-scale hydropower projects, there is enormous potential to expand the deployment of other renewable energy options such as solar, wind, geothermal and ocean-based energy sources\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-104">[104]</a></sup> The European Union has funded the Renewable Energy in Pacific Island Countries Developing Skills and Capacity programme (EPIC). Since its inception in 2013, the programme has developed a master&#8217;s programme in renewable energy management at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="University of Papua New Guinea">University of Papua New Guinea</a> and helped to establish a Centre of Renewable Energy at the same university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-5"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Papua New Guinea is one of the 15 beneficiaries of a programme on Adapting to Climate Change and Sustainable Energy worth &#8364;37.26 million. The programme resulted from the signing of an agreement in February 2014 between the European Union and the Pacific Islands Forum Secretariat. The other beneficiaries are the Cook Islands, Fiji, Kiribati, Marshall Islands, Federated States of Micronesia, Nauru, Niue, Palau, Samoa, Solomon Islands, Timor-Leste, Tonga, Tuvalu and Vanuatu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-6"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Transport in Papua New Guinea">Transport in Papua New Guinea</a></div>\n<p>Transport in Papua New Guinea is heavily limited by the country\'s mountainous terrain. As a result, air travel is the single most important form of transport for human and high density/value freight. Airplanes made it possible to open up the country during its early colonial period. Even today the two largest cities, <a href="/wiki/Port_Moresby" title="Port Moresby">Port Moresby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lae" title="Lae">Lae</a>, are only directly connected by planes. Port Moresby is not linked by road to any of the other major towns, and many remote villages can only be reached by light aircraft or on foot.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jacksons_International_Airport" title="Jacksons International Airport">Jacksons International Airport</a> is the major international airport in Papua New Guinea, located 8 kilometres (5&#160;mi) from Port Moresby. In addition to two international airfields, Papua New Guinea has 578 airstrips, most of which are unpaved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals"
